<div id="review_727779453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727779453" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727779453?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18488397-under-a-painted-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=penguin">penguin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727779453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13805806530754889821">First thing you need to know about this book: there are cowboys. Second thing you need to know: it's really well researched. And third thing: it's SO FUN.<br/><br/>I honestly don't think I've ever read a YA book like this one. There just aren't that many YA westerns out there. But this book embodies everything great about the genre and time period, with survivalist situations, outlaws, and dangerous animals. Also, did I mention the cowboys? Like, how often are there cowboys in YA? So cool!<br/><br/>Another great th</span>
  <span id="freeText13805806530754889821" style="display:none">First thing you need to know about this book: there are cowboys. Second thing you need to know: it's really well researched. And third thing: it's SO FUN.<br /><br />I honestly don't think I've ever read a YA book like this one. There just aren't that many YA westerns out there. But this book embodies everything great about the genre and time period, with survivalist situations, outlaws, and dangerous animals. Also, did I mention the cowboys? Like, how often are there cowboys in YA? So cool!<br /><br />Another great thing about this book is the cast of characters. I loved Samantha, our MC, and Annamae, the escaped slave; I also loved the three cowboys they start traveling with. Each had his or her own distinct personality, and they were all lovable. I especially loved Annamae. Like seriously, I want her to be my best friend.<br /><br />Because the MC is of Chinese descent, Stacey was able to add another layer of culture into the story. I loved how Samantha would talk about the years people were born and how that affected their personalities; it was fascinating. And it was really cool that Stacey stuck with that theme throughout the novel.<br /><br />Historical is one of my favorite genres, and I've read a lot of them. Western expansion is also my favorite time period in American history. I get frustrated with a lot of novels that I think rewrite the past, with characters that act and do things that they wouldn't have done back then, but Stacey's book never fell into that trap. She stays true to the time period and also the characters, and she almost makes me want to go back in time and travel with Samantha and her friends.<br /><br />...you know, except for the outlaws, the rattlesnakes, the disease, and the uncomfortable travel arrangements. ;-)<br /><br />Read this book if you're looking for your next page turner. Its pacing is fast, its characters endearing, and shot of racial diversity just plain awesome. One of my favorite YA historicals for sure!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13805806530754889821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_835359680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/835359680" />
    <a title="Renée Ahdieh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5021803-ren-e-ahdieh"><img alt="Renée Ahdieh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487663207p2/5021803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835359680?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renée Ahdieh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renée Ahdieh" href="/user/show/5021803-ren-e-ahdieh">Renée Ahdieh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18488397-under-a-painted-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835359680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4894978051504217758">This is a gorgeous, gorgeous book. I want to jump in a DeLorean and go back in time so I can be Sammy's best friend (and admire West from a safe distance).<br/><br/>Stacey Lee is a beautiful writer with a unique voice and a superb eye for detail. The way in which she develops the relationships in the novel is nuanced and perfect.<br/><br/>I can't wait to see what she pens next.<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237035634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2987962801630724145">This is stunning. If it weren't for work and sleep, I would have read this all in one sitting. 'Under a Painted Sky' is such beautiful story. Each character was phenomenal, and I absolutely adore the friendship between Andy and Sammy. Plus, there was so much more action than I anticipated! This is definitely a book that grabs you straight from the first page. I recommend this to everyone! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1222769715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222769715" />
    <a title="Book Riot Community" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33447134-book-riot-community"><img alt="Book Riot Community" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583162430p2/33447134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1222769715?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Riot Community" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Riot Community" href="/user/show/33447134-book-riot-community">Book Riot Community</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33447134-book-riot-community?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222769715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17327675125087677562">When is the last time you read a feminist western in YA about friendship?<br/><br/>Lee’s debut novel is an utterly refreshing and exciting adventure story set during the Oregon Trail years. It begins when Samantha, a Chinese girl in St. Joseph, Missouri, experiences a tragic loss in her life and realizes that her dreams of moving back to New York City and pursing a career in music might never come to be.<br/><br/>It’s through chance she meets Annamae, a runaway slave, and together, the girls decide they’re going to</span>
  <span id="freeText17327675125087677562" style="display:none">When is the last time you read a feminist western in YA about friendship?<br /><br />Lee’s debut novel is an utterly refreshing and exciting adventure story set during the Oregon Trail years. It begins when Samantha, a Chinese girl in St. Joseph, Missouri, experiences a tragic loss in her life and realizes that her dreams of moving back to New York City and pursing a career in music might never come to be.<br /><br />It’s through chance she meets Annamae, a runaway slave, and together, the girls decide they’re going to head out West in order to meet up with people with whom they can begin their lives afresh. But because they stick out, the girls disguise themselves as boys, take on new names, and hook up with a rag tag group of cowboys also making their way along the Trail. The well-paced story is full of ups and downs, but what really pushes the narrative forward is the amazing relationship that grows between Sam and Andy. Sure, there’s a little romance between Sam and one of the cowboys, but through-and-through, this is about the intense and life-altering power of female friendship.<br /><br />My favorite part of this book? Samantha kills a full-grown man when he tries to take advantage of her. Maybe I shouldn’t be so excited about murder, but it was a hell of a scene in the book and ultimately showcased just how badass Samantha is. Buy this book as soon as it comes out. It’s outstanding YA.<br /><br /><br /><br />From Buy, Borrow, Bypass: Diverse Teen Girl Duos in YA <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookriot.com/2015/03/09/buy-borrow-bypass-ya-with-diverse-teen-girls/">http://bookriot.com/2015/03/09/buy-bo...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17327675125087677562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_962790014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/962790014" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/962790014?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18488397-under-a-painted-sky">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1714237-lauren">Lauren</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=why-am-i-just-now-reading-this">why-am-i-just-now-reading-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=wild-wild-west">wild-wild-west</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer962790014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10487913379289431695">Very similar to <i>Walk on Earth a Stranger</i>, except I think I may have liked this one better. And that has a lot to do with the pacing. Or the fact that I listened to the audiobook, and the narrator made it seem more lively. Not sure which. Maybe both.<br/><br/>But I'm not going to compare the two books. I do want to point out the thing that made me want to read/listen to this book in the first place, and that is Lauren's reference to <a href='http://lwlink3.linkwithin.com/api/click?format=go&jsonp=vglnk_14527124567959&key=8a69ede45b8445f6b533712ba9899ffb&libId=ijd3rlcx0100r7tw000DA4tm0iaeu&loc=http%3A%2F%2Fstarryeyedrevue.blogspot.com%2F&v=1&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.loveisnotatriangle.com%2F2016%2F01%2Fthe-kiss-of-destruction.html&ref=http%3A%2F%2Fstarryeyedrevue.blogspot.com%2F2015%2F12%2Fmore-than-three-things-to-love-about.html&title=***The%20Starry-Eyed%20Revue***&txt=The%20Kiss%20of%20Destruction' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kiss of Destruction</a>. I don't <i>seek</i> out love triangles or romance drama </span>
  <span id="freeText10487913379289431695" style="display:none">Very similar to <i>Walk on Earth a Stranger</i>, except I think I may have liked this one better. And that has a lot to do with the pacing. Or the fact that I listened to the audiobook, and the narrator made it seem more lively. Not sure which. Maybe both.<br /><br />But I'm not going to compare the two books. I do want to point out the thing that made me want to read/listen to this book in the first place, and that is Lauren's reference to <a href="http://lwlink3.linkwithin.com/api/click?format=go&amp;jsonp=vglnk_14527124567959&amp;key=8a69ede45b8445f6b533712ba9899ffb&amp;libId=ijd3rlcx0100r7tw000DA4tm0iaeu&amp;loc=http%3A%2F%2Fstarryeyedrevue.blogspot.com%2F&amp;v=1&amp;out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.loveisnotatriangle.com%2F2016%2F01%2Fthe-kiss-of-destruction.html&amp;ref=http%3A%2F%2Fstarryeyedrevue.blogspot.com%2F2015%2F12%2Fmore-than-three-things-to-love-about.html&amp;title=***The%20Starry-Eyed%20Revue***&amp;txt=The%20Kiss%20of%20Destruction" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Destruction</a>. I don't <i>seek</i> out love triangles or romance drama per se, but just seeing how she actually <i>liked</i> the portrayal of the betrayal in this book -- and we all know how much she hates her triangular romances -- made me want to see why. And I agree, it is a great depiction of how the Kiss of Destruction can be employed without ruining the entire romance.<br /><br />But I loved this book for so much more than that. It was the camaraderie...the kinship the group found out on the open plains. This book just had so much heart, betrayal or not. The romance was so secondary to me that even if the love interest had been a cad about it, I could have overlooked it. The story itself was that good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10487913379289431695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1234307472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234307472" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_1251523132" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251523132" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251523132?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251523132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16931036447954084662"><i>
  <b>Life just tastes sweeter after you’ve licked death.</b>
</i><br/><br/>Two young ladies, one a fifteen-year-old Chinese girl whose father died recently in a fire, and one an African girl who is running from the chains of slavery, team up and disguise themselves as boys on an epic journey through the wild west where they meet a dashing band of cowboys and encounter numerous dangers.<br/><br/>Probably my favorite thing about <i>Under a Painted Sky</i> was the group of slightly wacky main characters and their hilarious conversatio</span>
  <span id="freeText16931036447954084662" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Life just tastes sweeter after you’ve licked death.</b>
</i><br /><br />Two young ladies, one a fifteen-year-old Chinese girl whose father died recently in a fire, and one an African girl who is running from the chains of slavery, team up and disguise themselves as boys on an epic journey through the wild west where they meet a dashing band of cowboys and encounter numerous dangers.<br /><br />Probably my favorite thing about <i>Under a Painted Sky</i> was the group of slightly wacky main characters and their hilarious conversations with each other. The dialogue had me cracking up every few pages and there were so many funny scenes that it would be impossible for me to pick a single favorite one.<br /><br />The western setting was wonderful. I loved how the cowboys West, Peety, and Cay (short for cayenne pepper) took it upon themselves to train Sammy and Andy to be "proper cowboys." Of course, this resulted in some truly hilarious incidents.<br /><br />Sammy frequently made references to her Chinese ancestry and some of her father's ancient Chinese traditions, which mixed surprisingly well with the western aspect of the book. <b>It created a unique and diverse atmosphere.</b><br /><br />I also loved the inclusion of spirituality. The characters freely talked about God and Sammy referenced to Jesus and heaven all the time in her thoughts. This made me happy and not just because I'm a Christian myself, but because it was historically accurate for the time era (when most people were Christians). The subject of religion also played for some good laughs on more than one occasion, which was a great way to lighten up the mood.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>It occurs to me that maybe God is in charge of the stars, after all. Maybe He has been saving Andy from the horrors of her life, little by little each day, and perhaps the trouble ahead isn’t so bad as the trouble she left behind.</b>
</i><br /><br />This book contained some seriously awesome messages about <b>the power of friendship and standing up for yourself.</b> The latter point was strongly emphasized because of the main characters' ethnic backgrounds. It's a sad fact that Chinese and black people weren't exactly the most popular in America in the 1800's. However, Sammy and Andy's <b>courageous spirits and positive attitudes</b> during these unfair times were truly admirable.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Maybe what matters is not so much the path as who walks beside you.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Fantastic, exciting, and funny with just a touch of romance.</b> Stacey Lee had a really great writing style that flowed from page to page. I'm looking forward to reading more from her in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16931036447954084662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1233678454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1233678454" />
    <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love"><img alt="nick (the infinite limits of love)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606193187p2/2993271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1233678454?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nick (the infinite limits of love)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nick (the infinite limits of love)" href="/user/show/2993271-nick-the-infinite-limits-of-love">nick (the infinite limits of love)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1233678454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6479122096347131090"><br/>The book publishing industry is already winning at 2015 with all the diverse books that are being released. Stacey Lee's Under a Painted Sky not only shines because of the diversity that it explores, but it's also a stunningly written book that captivated me from the very start.<br/><br/>Under a Painted Sky was more than anything, a story about friendship and about two girls finding strength in each other. It was a beautiful and touching story, and I couldn't help but fall in love with these two character</span>
  <span id="freeText6479122096347131090" style="display:none"><br />The book publishing industry is already winning at 2015 with all the diverse books that are being released. Stacey Lee's Under a Painted Sky not only shines because of the diversity that it explores, but it's also a stunningly written book that captivated me from the very start.<br /><br />Under a Painted Sky was more than anything, a story about friendship and about two girls finding strength in each other. It was a beautiful and touching story, and I couldn't help but fall in love with these two characters. Sammy, our Chinese protagonist, was a memorable character in many different ways. Perhaps, however, what truly drew me to her character was that inner resilience. Sammy was a gorgeously written character and a lot of her beauty in Under a Painted Sky came from her unwillingness to back down no matter what the obstacle that she faced. By her side was, a slave girl with a huge heart, Annamae. The bond that developed between these two young women was so much more than just a simple friendship. It was a sisterhood, where they took care of each other, disregarding their differences and sticking together through thick and thin. This delightful slow growing friendship between Sammy and Annamae was the highlight of Under a Painted Sky for me, at times, even making me jealous because I envied their emotional connection.<br /><br />The friendship between Sammy and Annamae wasn't the only friendship that developed throughout the book. Another wonderful friendship started brewing between Sammy, Annamae, and the three adorable cowboys that they encounter while the girls, pretending to be boys to escape the authorities, are on the Oregon Trail. The three cowboys, Cay, West and Peety, were a delightful. The dynamics between them was such a blast for me. Characterizations weren't the only elements of Under a Painted Sky that blew me away. Stacey Lee's writing and world building were equally amazing. With Under a Painted Sky, the author transported me to the times and her vivid writing was an emotional experience in itself. I was so invested in the book that I actually wound up being petrified for these characters because of all the dangers they encountered, both natural and from other people. The author did a fabulous job at describing the time period and making me experience it as if I was there myself.<br /><br />Under the Painted Sky was one truly beautifully written book heavy on themes of diversity and friendship. This is one of 2015's strongest debuts and you all HAVE to experience Stacey Lee's lovely writing style and wonderful characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6479122096347131090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2377815795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377815795" />
    <a title="Namera [The Literary Invertebrate]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate"><img alt="Namera [The Literary Invertebrate]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587154687p2/31792110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377815795?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Namera [The Literary Invertebrate]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Namera [The Literary Invertebrate]" href="/user/show/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate">Namera [The Literary Invertebrate]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate?shelf=genderbender">genderbender</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate?shelf=ow-drama">ow-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31792110-namera-the-literary-invertebrate?shelf=poc-heroine">poc-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377815795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer722981540561513702">I first read this book when it came out four years ago and I remembered enjoying it, so I randomly decided to do a reread. <b>
  <u>It isn’t perfect – especially in the realm of the romance – but it was good fun</u>
</b>, hence the generous rating.<br/><br/>Fifteen-year-old <b>Samantha Young</b> (yes, she’s a lot younger than I’m used to in YA) lives in Missouri with her widowed father. They own a general store and they’re eking out a living, even if the attitudes of their neighbours leave a lot to be desired. Chinese people </span>
  <span id="freeText722981540561513702" style="display:none">I first read this book when it came out four years ago and I remembered enjoying it, so I randomly decided to do a reread. <b>
  <u>It isn’t perfect – especially in the realm of the romance – but it was good fun</u>
</b>, hence the generous rating.<br><br>Fifteen-year-old <b>Samantha Young</b> (yes, she’s a lot younger than I’m used to in YA) lives in Missouri with her widowed father. They own a general store and they’re eking out a living, even if the attitudes of their neighbours leave a lot to be desired. Chinese people aren’t having the best time in 1849 America; Sam desperately wants to go back to New York and become a musician, but her father keeps telling her to wait it out.<br><br>Then disaster strikes. Her father dies in a fire, and rather than helping out, their landlord tries to force Sam to join his brothel as a prostitute. She kills him when he tries to rape her and flees with the help of a runaway slave girl named <b>Annamae</b>. Disguised as boys to throw pursuers off their scent, the pair soon fall into companionship with a group of three cowboys. White cousins <b>West and Cayenne Pepper</b> (seriously), together with a Hispanic man named <b>Peety</b>, take the pair of ‘boys’ under their wing. What follows is a pretty light-hearted tale of friendship and romance.<br><br>It was in fact surprisingly light-hearted. For the most part there’s no graphic violence – not even the scene where Sam accidentally kills her landlord – and I definitely got the impression that I was reading a ‘sanitised’ version of a Wild West story. Where were the blood, sweat, and tears? Don’t get me wrong, though: I appreciated the touches of humour, and stories of girls disguised as boys are always entertaining.<br><br>The best thing by far about this book is the friendship between Sam and Annamae. As a Chinese and black girl respectively, they obviously know what it’s like to be on the outskirts of society (though of course, it’s acknowledged that Annamae is the only one whose race actually makes her a slave). <b>Their love and loyalty for each other shone through in every interaction.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>The weakest thing about this book is the romance.</u>
</b> We barely know anything about West; he’s just the dark-haired, brooding artist boy to Cay’s flirtatious blondness. I definitely thought we learned way more about Cay, and I preferred him in many ways. There’s also an irritating scene where West has sex with another girl because he’s conflicted about his feelings for someone Chinese. I definitely could have done without that, though I suppose it’s fair enough that an 1849 boy wouldn’t willingly fall for a non-white.<br><br><b>
  <u>The ending was kind of a copout</u>
</b>; it felt very abrupt and didn’t tie up most of the loose ends in the novel. The book definitely should have been longer. Still, it was a good debut and I love the easy flow of Lee’s writing, so I can’t wait for her next novel this summer! I like that she focuses on the diverse aspects of history, and this book was one of the earliest ones to do so.<br><br><a href="http://www.theliteraryinvertebrate.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">[Blog]</a> - <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_literary_invertebrate/" rel="nofollow noopener">[Bookstagram]</a><br><br><a href="http://s1376.photobucket.com/user/theliteraryinvertebrate/media/c%20l%20i%20m%20b%20C2A0e%20v%20e%20r%20y%20C2A0m%20o%20u%20n%20t%20a%20i%20n%202_zpsykn9gbgr.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533226812i/26067187._SX540_.png" alt=" photo c l i m b C2A0e v e r y C2A0m o u n t a i n 2_zpsykn9gbgr.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="722981540561513702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6mwdr1MZbJgn/PkQy9MUOjyO7+Yy+C13LMX2jHUjgRbhwqdt7xtyTEE3bCCsKFB9byTMek7MeyzlTW31IwbLyA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uJMfQvdWNxe5J1CUsopevxqJGkijkUO+W32ldOuNPZ6zPaWAS1Qpw9/sxaTVcRr4SSM51N+lFeWS9T4Nvah3QA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13151430118941117364">Stacey Lee is a fourth generation Chinese-American whose people came to California during the heydays of the cowboys. She believes she still has a bit of cowboy dust in her soul. A native of southern California, she graduated from UCLA then got her law degree at UC Davis King Hall. After practicing law in the Silicon Valley for several years, she finally took up the pen because she wanted the perk</span>
  <span id="freeText13151430118941117364" style="display:none">Stacey Lee is a fourth generation Chinese-American whose people came to California during the heydays of the cowboys. She believes she still has a bit of cowboy dust in her soul. A native of southern California, she graduated from UCLA then got her law degree at UC Davis King Hall. After practicing law in the Silicon Valley for several years, she finally took up the pen because she wanted the perks of being able to nap during the day, and it was easier than moving to Spain. She plays classical piano, raises children, and writes YA fiction.<br /></span>
